The Third Proof: Orderly Transformation Requires a Wise Creator
Razi presents the third proof from orderly transformation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's argument that the orderly transformation of a sperm-drop into a human body cannot be caused by the human or its parents, and therefore requires a wise external creator.

Core Idea
Orderly change demands an external wise cause, not the object itself or its natural origins.

Imam al-Razi presents the third proof for the existence of a wise Creator, focusing on the observable changes in biological development. He uses the example of the transformation from sperm into a fully formed human to argue that this process demands an influencer beyond the human and its parents. This lesson introduces that proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Razi starts with the observed transformation (sperm → clot → lump → flesh/bones).
The transformation is a clear example of 'accidents' or changes.
2
Identify the logical steps
Identify the three key claims: (1) transformation needs an influencer, (2) not the human or parents, (3) so something else (a wise creator) must be the cause.
3
Reflect on the necessity of an external cause
Ask yourself why the human or parents cannot be the cause. The commentary explains that the human does not consciously control this process, and the parents' role ends at conception.
This points to a separate, wise agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطريق الثالث : حدوث الأعراض مثل ما لشاهده من انقلاب النطفة علقة ثم معنفة ثم لا اودما فلا بد من مور ، وليس المؤثر هو الإنسان ولا أبواه ولابد من شيء آخر .
لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر هو القوة المولدة المركوزة في النطاقة .
لانا نقول : تلك القوة إما أن يكون لها شعور واختيار في التكرين وإما أن لا يكون ، والأول باطل وإلا لكانت النطقة موصوفة بكمال القدرة والحكمة وهو معلوم الفساد بالبديهة ، و الثانى أيضاً باطل لأن النطفة إما أن تكون جسما متشابه الأجزاء في الحقيقة وإما أن لا تكون كذلك ، فإن كان الأول لزم أن يخلق النطفة كرة لأن القوة البسيطة إذا أثرت في المادة البسيطة لابد وأن تفعل فعلا متشابها وهو الكرة وهذا هو الذي عليه تحويل الفلاسفة فى كرية البائط، وإن كان الثانى كانت النطفة مركبة من البسائط وكل واحد من تلك البائط يكون القائم بها قوة بسيطة وذلك يقتضى الكروية فيلزم أن تتخلق النطفة كرات مضموم بعضها إلى البعض ، ولما بطل ذلك علينا أن المؤثر فى خلق أبدان الحيوانات والنبات مؤثر حكيم .
The third way: the occurrence of accidents, like what is witnessed from the transformation of the sperm-drop into a clot, then into a chewed lump, then into flesh and bones? So there must be an influencer, and the influencer is not the human nor his parents, and there must be something else. It cannot be said: why is it not permissible that the influencer be the generative power embedded in the sperm-drop? For we say: that power either has consciousness and choice in the formation or not. The first is false, otherwise the sperm-drop would be described with complete power and wisdom, and that is known to be false intuitively. The second is also false, because the sperm-drop either is a body similar in parts in reality or not. If the first, then the sperm-drop would be created as a sphere, because a simple power, when it acts on a simple matter, must produce a similar action, which is the sphere, and this is what the philosophers have transmitted regarding the sphericity of the simple? If the second, then the sperm-drop is composed of simples, and each of those simples has a simple power subsisting in it, and that necessitates sphericity, so it would follow that the sperm-drop is created as spheres attached to one another. And when that is invalidated, it is incumbent on us that the influencer in the creation of the bodies of animals and plants is a wise influencer.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof (الطريق الثالث) for the existence of a wise Creator, which is based on the occurrence of accidents (حدوث الأعراض). The proof uses the example of the transformation of a sperm-drop (نطفة) into a clot (علقة), then into a chewed lump (مضغة), and then into flesh and bones. This orderly transformation requires an external influencer (مؤثر), and neither the human nor its parents are the cause; therefore, there must be another agent. The author then anticipates an objection: why not attribute this to a 'generative power' (قوة مولدة) inherent in the sperm? He refutes this by analyzing the nature of that power. If it had consciousness and choice, the sperm would have to be endowed with perfect power and wisdom, which is obviously false. If it lacked consciousness, then the sperm, being either homogeneous or composite, would produce a spherical shape (a simple action from a simple power) or multiple spheres, which is not what we observe. Since neither scenario yields the observed complex and orderly forms, the only remaining conclusion is that the actual influencer is a wise external agent.

Key Terms
حدوث الأعراض
النطفة
المؤثر الحكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why cannot the human be the cause of its own transformation from sperm?
A) Because the human is not yet conscious at that stage.
B) Because the transformation happens after the human is born.
C) Because the human has no power over its own development.
D) Because the human is not present at the time of transformation.

Key Takeaway
The orderly transformation from sperm to human cannot be self-caused or caused by parents; it demands a wise external creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever truly contemplated the miracle of your own existence—that you were once a sperm-drop, then a clot, then a chewed lump? How does this realization confront your pride and self-sufficiency? What specific act of gratitude can you perform today to acknowledge that you did not create yourself?
?
If the orderly transformation of your body is undeniable proof of a wise Creator, then what about the 'accidents' (changes) in your life—your successes, failures, and unexpected turns? Are you quick to attribute them to your own planning or to other people, rather than to the wise influencer? Which area of your life do you most need to submit to His wisdom right now?
?
Razi eliminates both the human and the parents as the true cause of your formation. How does this strip away your excuses for ingratitude? If you were not the author of even your own physical existence, what claim do you have over anything you 'achieve'? Will you commit today to starting each morning with a renewed acknowledgment that every transformation in your life is from Him?
